HOW TO USE THE AUTO/TRUCK KEY BLANK REFERENCE
1. Two indexes are provided; the MANUFACTURER INDEX and the MODEL INDEX. Both indexes are 
in alphabetical order. The Manufacturer Index references brands like Toyota, Dodge and BMW. The 
model index lists models like the Camry (Toyota), Ram (Dodge) and 3 Series (BMW). Both indexes 
tell the user on what page the reference information will be found.
2. The body of the Reference explains Manufacturer, Model, Years, Lock Applications (i.e. ignition, 
door/truck, etc.) and Code Series.  The Ilco/EZ number is the key number. A [P] indicates the key 
is available with a plastic head and a [PC] indicates the key is available in various plastic colors.  
The Transponder Information column provides pertinent information to producing the transponder 
key such as special equipment or which on board program (OBP) should be used. The Substitutes 
column provides other key blanks that should work in the application if the referenced key blank is 
not available and the Notes column contains information to assist you in cutting the key. 
In the 2023 Ilco Auto/Truck Reference Guide is a column for Card No. In this column, users of our 
Futura, Ilco EZ®-Code, Ultracode, Tri Code H.S., Triax and Universal II code machine products will 
• Where no card number is given, either a suitable card number does not exist, or the key in 
question cannot be cut on the above listed equipment. 
• Where more than one card number is listed, more than one possible card exists; the correct 
card is dependent upon the key blank number required for the vehicle in question.
• In rare instances (the Kia section includes an example), in order to conform with code 
information as originally released by a manufacturer,  the Ilco card number requires reverse 
order depth numbering; in other words, the smaller depth bit numbers are deeper cuts than 
the larger depth bit numbers. On affected cards, if your source for bitting information utilized 
conventional depth numbering (smallest depth number = shallowest cut), you will have to 
invert their depth numbers before using the listed card number. Ilco has no control over how 
others publish code information, and assumes no liability for keys miscut as a result. 
 3. CLONING QUICK REFERENCE - A list of the vehicles/models known to  incorporate transponder 
technology that use an RW4 Plus / Ilco EZ ®-Clone device.
4. TRANSPONDER ON-BOARD PROGRAMMING PROCEDURES - This section explains the 
on-board programming procedures for installing the GM, Ford, Mazda, Toyota, Lexus and Chrysler 
programmable transponder keys that are referenced in the Auto/Truck.
5. TRANSPONDER KEYS - Actual size drawings of all transponder keys
6. 
By learning to use this reference, you can reduce the confusion over which key blank to use in an  
automobile or truck. Recognize that there will be exceptions to what is considered standard. Before cutting 
a replacement key, always compare the key blank to be cut with the original key.
IMPORTANT: Before ordering key blanks for your key boards, reference the Notes Column to see if 
the key blank is a High Security Key and requires a special key machine.  Be certain you have the key 
machine to cut the key before ordering the key blanks.
This book is provided as a service and is intended for reference only. Kaba Ilco Corp. disclaims liability for any damage or action resulting from the use of this 
information.

VIN CONVERSION (Vehicle Identification Number)
The VIN plate is located on the front of the dashboard on the drivers (LH) side of the vehicle, and is visible 
by looking into the vehicle through the windshield.
It is always important to verify the country of origin and the model year the vehicle was manufactured, 
and this is especially important when working on vehicles that require/could require transponder keys.  
1 K 3 L P 2 5 R S 2 1 3 2 4 3 0 0
TYPICAL VIN

2 – Canada
3 – Mexico

5 – USA
6 – Australia
J – Japan
K – Korea
L – China,Taiwan

PROGRAMMING PROCEDURES
TRANSPONDER ON-BOARD PROGRAMMING PROCEDURES
Originate New Master Key
 1.  Insert new key 
into ignition cylinder and turn it to the ON (RUN) position. The security light 
on	the	dash	will	flash	for	fifteen	minutes.
	 2. 		When	the	security	light	stops	flashing,	you	have	five	minutes	to	start	the	next	step.	Turn	
the ignition cylinder OFF and then back to the  ON (RUN) 
position. The security light on 
the	dash	will	flash	for	fifteen	more	minutes.	
	 3. 		When	the	security	light	stops	flashing,	you	have	five	minutes	to	start	the	next	step.	Turn	
the ignition cylinder to OFF and then back to the ON  (RUN) position. 
The security light on 
the	dash	will	flash	for	fifteen	more	minutes.
	 4. 		After	the	security	light	stops	flashing	the	third	time,	the	new	key	has	been	programmed	into	
the vehicles computer and will operate 
the car. It has replaced ALL  the previous electronic 
key codes and is the ONLY key programmed into the vehicle’s computer.
Add Duplicate key
 1.  Insert an existing key into the ignition cylinder.
 2.  Turn the ignition cylinder to ON (RUN) and back to OFF.
	
3.		Remove	the	existing	key	and,	within	fifteen	seconds,	insert	the	new	key	and	turn	it	to	ON	
(RUN).
 4.  The security light will light up for two seconds to indicate 
success in programming the key 
into the vehicle.
1997 Ford, LincoLn, Mercury
1998 Ford, Mercury
Originate New Master Key
 1. Insert new key into ignition cylinder and turn 
it to the ON (RUN) position. The security light 
on the dash will illuminate and stay on for ten minutes.
 2. When the security light goes out, you have one minute to start the next step. Turn the ignition 
cylinder to OFF and then back to the ON (RUN) 
position. The security light on the dash will 
illuminate and stay on for ten more minutes.
 3. When the security light goes out, you have one minute to start the next step. Turn the ignition 
cylinder to OFF and then back on the ON 
(RUN) position. The security light on the dash 
will illuminate and stay on for ten more minutes. 
 4. After the security light has gone off the third time, the key has been programmed into the 
vehicle’s computer and will operate the car. It has replaced 
ALL the previous electronic key 
codes and is the ONLY key programmed into the vehicle’s computer.
Add Duplicate Key
 1. Insert an existing key into the ignition cylinder.
 2. Turn the ignition cylinder to ON (RUN) and back to OFF.
	
3.	Remove	the	existing	key	and,	within	fifteen	seconds,	insert	the	new	key	and	turn	it	to	ON	
(RUN).
 4. The security light will light up for two seconds 
to indicate success in programming the key 
into the vehicle.
If the Add Duplicate key instructions above did not work follow the variation below.
 1. Insert already programmed key into ignition and START car.
 2. Turn key off and remove key.
 3. Insert key to be programmed and turn to ON within 15 seconds of removing the already 
programmmed key.
 4. The security light will go off once the key has been programmed.
 5. Remove key and then test.
If the vehicle doesn’t have a security 
light, leave the key in for 10 minutes and 30 seconds during 
step 4.

PROGRAMMING PROCEDURES
The on-board programming procedures for the Mazda 626 should be used only if the preferred 
methods are unavailable. The Mazda dealers use a New Generation Star Tester to originate and 
add new duplicate keys to this model vehicle.
The ILCO RW2 or RW2, RW3, RW4/EZ-Clone should be used for these purposes by Ilco dealers. 
The following procedures will require pre-programmed keys. Ilco transponder keys fo Mazda are not 
available pre-programmed
Originate New Master Key or Add Duplicate Key
 1. Insert new key into ignition cylinder and turn it to the ON (RUN) position. Turn back to the 
LOCK	position.	Repeat	until	this	has	been	done	five	times.	Do	not	let	the	lock	sit	for	more	
than one second in any position during this step.
 2. Turn the key back to the ON  (RUN) position. The dash mounted security light should be 
flashing	rapidly.	Within	twenty	seconds	turn	to	the	LOCK	position	and	leave	it	there	for	five	
minutes.	After	this	five	minute	delay,	the	security	light	should	slow	to	a	much	slower	rate.
 3.  Within twenty seconds, enter the code password.
 4.  The code password is obtained by supplying the vehicle’s 
Immobilizer Unit serial number to 
Mazda. It is an eight digit number unique to each Immobilizer Unit.
 5.  While carefully watching the dash mounted security 
light, turn the ignition to the ON (RUN) 
position.	Count	the	number	of	flashes	by	the	security	light	and	turn	back	to	LOCK	when	the	
number	of	flashes	equals	the	first	digit	of	the	password.
 6. Within thirty seconds,  turn the ignition lock back to ON (RUN) and count until the number of 
flashes	matches	the	value	of	the	second	digit	of	the	password.	Turn	the	ignition	lock	back	
to LOCK.
 7.  Repeat until all eight password digits have been entered. Use caution and turn the lock 
from one position to the other only when the security light is NOT 
illuminated. If a mistake 
is	made	or	the	count	of	flashes	is	lost,	wait	forty-five	seconds	and	start	over.
	 8. 		When	the	security	light	stops	flashing	and	stays	illuminated,	the	password	has	been	
entered correctly.
 9.  Start the vehicle and the security light should go off within two seconds.
 10. Additional new keys may be added by inserting them and starting the car within twenty 
seconds of removing the previous key.
 11.  Thirty seconds after the last key has been removed, the vehicle will end the program mode 
and return to normal operating mode.
1998 Mazda 626
E
D
The Toyota Electronic Control Module does not have programming modes without a pre-pro-
grammed key. If there is no key available that is already programmed into the module, the module 
must be replaced.
To delete all but one key from the unit
 1. Simultaneously depress and release brake and accelerator pedals 1 time.
 2. Insert an 
existing master key into the ignition cylinder.Do not turn the key from the OFF 
(LOCK) position.
	 3.	 Within	fifteen	seconds	of	inserting	the	key,	depress	and	release	the	accelerator	pedal	six	
times.
 4. Within twenty seconds of completing the above step, depress 
and release the brake pedal 
seven times.
	 5.	 The	security	light	will	flash,	indicating	all	keys	other	than	the	one	being	used	have	been	
deleted.
 6. Remove the key from the ignition cyli
nder within ten seconds. It will be the only key still 
programmed to work.
Add Duplicate Key
 1. Simultaneously depress and release brake and accelerator pedals 1 time.
 2. Insert existing master key into ignition.
 3. Within 15 seconds depress and release accelerator pedal 5 times.
 4. Within 20 seconds depress and release the brake pedal 6 times and remove key.
 5. Within 10 seconds insert new key into ignition.
 6. Within 10 seconds depress and release the accelerator pedal 1 time.
 7. After 80 seconds new key is registered and security light goes off.
 8. Remove new key and depress and release brake pedal 1 time.

PROGRAMMING PROCEDURES
Originate New Master Key
 1.  This requires the vehicle to be connected to special dealer diagnostic
 equipment.
Add Duplicate Key - Must have two programmed 
Sentry Keys
 1.  Insert one of the two valid keys into the ignition lock and turn to the ON (RUN) position.
	
2.		After	the	key	has	been	in	the	ON	position	for	at	least	five	seconds,	but	no	more	than	15	 
seconds turn the lock back to OFF.
 3.  Remove the key and insert the second valid key and turn to the ON position within 15  
seconds.	(The	second	key	must	not	be	the	same	as	the	first	key.)
 4.  A theft alarm light should illuminate after ten seconds and a single chime sound will indicate 
entry into the Customer Programming Mode.
 5.  Turn the key to the OFF position within 60 seconds and remove the valid key.
 6.  Insert a new key and turn to the ON position.
 7.  After approximately ten 
seconds, a single chime will sound and the theft alarm light will 
stop.	
	Wait	five	seconds	and	turn	to	the	OFF	position.
 8.  The above steps must be repeated for additional keys.

Originate New Master Key
 Master Keys must be used.
 1.  Make proper cuts onto a GM Master key.
 2.  Insert the new working key into 
the ignition cylinder and turn it to the ON position. The 
THEFT light will light up and stay on for about 10 minutes.
 3.  When the light goes out, repeat the same procedure as in step #2, two more times.
 4.  When the THEFT light goes out, the new key has been programmed.
 To program the second key.
	 1. 		Within	20	seconds	of	completing	the	last	step	for	the	first	key,	insert	a	second	Master	key	
and turn to the ON position. When the light goes out, the new key is programmed.
 2.  Repeat the previous step for programming up to 12 additional keys.
Add Duplicate Key - Must have two programmed Sentry Keys
	 1.		Insert	the	first	working	key	into	the	ignition	cylinder.
 2.  Turn the ignition cylinder to the ON position.
 3.  When the SECURITY light goes out, remove the key.
 4.  Insert the second working key and turn the ignition cylinder ON.
 5.  When the SECURITY light goes out, remove the key.
 6.  Insert the new duplicate key and turn the ignition cylinder 
ON.
 7.  When the SECURITY light goes out, key has been programmed.

to disconnect the battery for 10 
minutes, and then continue with the 3 x 10.45 On Board Procedure

H
Originate New Master Key
 1. This requires that the vehicle be connected to special 
diagnostic equipment (TKO/SDD). 
There are two ten minute delays involved while this device erases all existing key program-
ming and sets up the vehicle computer to accept new key codes. Two new keys should 
be ready because the system requires a minimum of two keys in the program. After the 
first	two	keys	are	programmed,	additional	keys	can	be	entered	individually	by	following	the	
instructions for adding duplicate keys.
Add Duplicate Key (Requires two working keys)
 1. Insert an existing key into the ignition cylinder.
 2. Turn the ignition cylinder to ON (RUN) 
and back to OFF.
	 3. 	Remove	the	existing	key	and,	within	five	seconds,	insert	a	second	key	and	turn	it	to	ON	
(RUN) then back OFF.
 4. Insert the new key before ten seconds have elapsed  and turn it to ON (RUN). Leave it on 
for one second and turn back to OFF.
 5. The security light will light up for three seconds to indicate 
that the new key has been 
successfully programmed.
 6. Once the key has been successfully 
programmed, do not remove the key from the ignition 
cylinder. The key must be left in the cylinder for approximately 10 minutes before the pro-
gramming procedure is complete. Should someone attempt to start the vehicle or remove 
the key from the ignition cylinder prior to the 10 minutes elapsing, the keys will not function 
correctly and the programming procedure will have to be carried out again.

2002+ ToyoTa, Lexus
J Add Duplicate Key (Requires two working keys)
 1. Insert an existing key into the ignition cylinder.
 2. Turn the ignition cylinder 
to ON (RUN) for at least 3 seconds, but no more than 10 seconds, 
and then back to OFF.
 3. Remove the existing key, and within 10 seconds 
insert a second key, turning it ON (RUN) 
for at least 3 seconds, but no more than 10 seconds and then back to OFF.
 4. Remove the second key, and within 20 seconds, insert the new, un-programmed key into 
the ignition
 cylinder.
 
 5. Turn the new key to ON (RUN) for at least 6 seconds and then turn back to OFF.
 6. The security light 
will illuminate for up to 3 seconds to indicate that the new key has been 
successfully	programmed.	
	A	flashing	security	light	will	indicate	unsuccessful	programming.
 7. If the key has been successfully programmed, it will start the vehicle’
s engines as well as 
operate the remote entry system.
Ford/LincoLn/Mercury ikT
K Add Duplicate Key (Requires two working keys)
 1. Insert and existing key into the ignition cylinder.
 2. Turn the ignition cylinder to ON (RUN) 
for approximately 3 seconds and then back to 
OFF. 
 3. Remove the existing key, and within 10 seconds 
insert a second key, turning it ON (RUN) 
for approximately 3 seconds, and then back to OFF.
 4. Remove the second key, and within 10 seconds, insert the new, un-programmed key into 
the ignition
 cylinder.
 5. Turn the new key ON (RUN) for approximately 
3 seconds and then back to OFF.
 6. Repeat steps 1-5 for each additional key.  A total of 8 keys can be programmed.
Programming Remote Keyless Entry (RKE)
 1. Unlock the door locks, using the door lock control switch.
 2. Within 6 seconds, 
turn the ignition cylinder from OFF to On (RUN) 4 times, with the fourth 
time ending in OFF.
 3. Within 10 seconds, press any button on the RKE to be programmed.  
 4. Press any button on each of the subsequent RKE’s to be programmed.  A total of 8 RKE’s 
can be programmed.
 5. Exiting the programming mode can be accomplished by turning the ignition cylinder to the 
ON	(RUN)	position,	waiting	10	seconds	after	the	final	RKE	has	been	programmed,	or	by	
reaching the maximum 8 RKE’s that can be programmed.

L Add Duplicate Key (Requires two working keys)

n cylinder.

Programming Remote Keyless Entry (RKE)
 1. The front doors must be closed and unlocked 
before proceeding.
 2. Within 6 seconds, turn the ignition 
cylinder from OFF to On (RUN) 4 times, with the fourth 
time ending in OFF.  If the module successfully enters programming mode you will hear a 
chime.
 3. Within 10 seconds, press 
any button on the RKE to be programmed.  You will hear a chime 
to indicate successful programming.  Repeat this step for each RKE to be programmed.  A 
total of 4 RKE’s can be programmed.
 4. Exiting the programming 
mode can be accomplished by turning the ignition cylinder to the 
ON	(RUN)	position,	waiting	10	seconds	after	the	final	RKE	has	been	programmed,	or	by	
reaching the maximum 8 RKE’s that can be programmed.

gM high securiTy key (norTh aMerica, excepT canada)
N Add New Transmitter (Requires one working transmitter)
 1. Insert an existing transmitter into the cupholder.
 2. Insert the key of the new transmitter into the driver’s 
side door lock, turning the key to the 
unlock position 5 times within 10 seconds.  The Driver Information Center will now display, 
Ready For Remote #2, 3, 4, or 5.
 3. Insert the new transmitter into the transmitter pocket.  The transmitter pocket is located 
inside the 
center console under the cupholder.  Remove the cupholder to access the trans-
mitter pocket.
 4. Press the ignition 
button.  Once the new transmitter has been programmed, the Driver 
Information Center will display that it is ready to program the next transmitter.
 5. Remove the new transmitter 
from the transmitter pocket and press the Unlock button on the 
transmitter.
 6. Repeat steps 3-5 to program additional transmitters.  Press and hold the ignition button for 
5 seconds to exit the programming mode.
Originate New Transmitter (No working transmitter exists)
 1. Insert the key of the new transmitter into the driver’s side door lock, turning the key to the 
unlock 
position 5 times within 10 seconds.  The Driver Information Center will now display, 
Remote Learn Pending, Please Wait.
 2. Wait ten minutes until the Driver Information Center displays, Press Engine Start Button 
to Learn and press the ignition button.  
The Driver Information Center will again display, 
Remote Learn Pending, Please Wait.
 3. Repeat Step 2 two additional times.  After 
the third time, all existing transmitters for the 
vehicle will no longer work the vehicle.  Any remaining transmitters can be re-learned .  The 
Driver Information Center will now display, Ready For Remote #1.
 4.  Insert the new transmitter into the transmitter pocket.  The transmitter pocket is located 
inside the 
center console under the cupholder.  Remove the cupholder to access the trans-
mitter pocket.
 5. Press the ignition button.  Once 
the new transmitter has been programmed, the Driver 
Information Center will display that it is ready to program the next transmitter.
 6. Remove the new transmitter 
from the transmitter pocket and press the Unlock button on the 
transmitter.
 7. Repeat steps 4-6 to program additional transmitters.  Press and hold the ignition button for 
5 seconds to exit the programming mode.

TKO/SDD Required Special Duplicator Required
Transponder Related Glossary Terms
SYSTEMS
Immobilizer System: System used in disarming vehicles when an improper or non-transponder key is used.  The first  
component disarmed in most systems is the Fuel Pump.
PATS: Passive Anti-Theft System  (Ford).
Securilock™: Name for Ford PATS System.
PASS Key® III: Personalized Automotive Security System (Registered Trademark - GM).
PASS Key® III+: Current generation (2004-05) of the PASS Key® III. 
Passive: Requires that the user do nothing to Arm or Disarm.  The system is automatic.
Fixed Code: The code required to start the vehicle does not change.
Rolling Code: This system is more complex.  Each time the ignition is turned on, the engine has started and the transponder 
code is checked by the vehicle computer memory, a new code is written to the transponder. This new code is required for the 
car to start the next time.
Challenge Response Code (Encrypted): This system is the most complex of those currently in use. Communication between 
the key and the ECM is encrypted in both directions (bi-directional encryption of data) and the code changes during every use. 
In most cases, Ilco offers a solution to this system.
SYSTEM COMPONENTS
Transponder: Radio Frequency (RF) Transmitter Responder reacting to an electrical impulse of a reader  
constituted by a surrounding antenna.
Electronic Control Module (ECM): The ECM, or on-board computer, in a vehicle with an immobilizer system has special 
software designed to work with the immobilizer.  The immobilizer can communicate only with an ECM, which it recognizes.
Control Module: The control module communicates with the transponder in the ignition key via the antenna ring, as well as 
with the ECM.  The control module sends a carrier frequency via the antenna ring.  The frequency can be changed to the best 
possible frequency if needed.  A fixed number of codes are contained in the memory and the Control module verifies that the 
correct code is being sent.
Antenna: The antenna has two functions.  It transmits the carrier frequency from the control module to the transponder and 
transmits a coded identification signal from the transponder to the control module.
TRANSPONDER CHIPS
Read-Only/Fixed Code: This type of chip is used on most original transponder keys.  The  code can be read, but it cannot 
be written over.
Read-Write/Fixed Code: This type of chip is used on Ilco after market keys.  The transponder code can be read and  
programmed over.
PT: This key suffix refers to Ilco replacement keys containing pre-programmed chips.
T1: This key suffix refers to a first generation pre-programmed Philips® read/write chip used mainly in Europe.
T2: This key suffix refers to a second generation pre-programmed Philips® read/write chip and is used on some Ilco replacement keys.
T3: This key suffix refers to a glass Texas Instruments® pre-programmed read only chip.
T4: This key suffix refers to a plastic wedge Texas Instruments® pre-programmed read only chip.
T5: This key suffix refers to a blank or neutral transponder contained in the key head. This is a read-write chip used in most Ilco 
replacement keys that are used in conjunction with the RW2 or RW2, RW3, RW4/Ilco EZ-Clone®-Clone.
T6: This key suffix refers to a blank with a Megamos® encrypted read only chip.
T14: This key suffix refers to a plastic wedge Philips® CAN encrypted (ID46) pre-programmed read only chip.
T24: This key suffix refers to a glass Megamos® CAN encrypted pre-programmed read only chip.
Texas Instruments® (TI): This chip manufacturer produces both plastic wedge and glass transponder chips.  Chips are  
read-only.  Texas Instruments® chips for Chrysler and Lincoln LS are encrypted (Challenge Response).
Megamos®: This chip manufacturer produces both plastic wedge and glass transponder chips.  The original chips are read only 
and used on manufacturers including Honda, Cadillac, Porsche, and Jaguar.  Ilco uses a T5 to emulate this chip.  
Philips®: This chip manufacturer produces read-only and read-write original chips.  Ilco uses a T2 or T5 to emulate original 
Philips.®  Primary applications of this chip in the USA are Cadillac Catera, BMW, Infiniti, Mazda, Nissan, Mercedes and Volvo.
Motorola™: This read only chip is only used on one model, the Lincoln Mark VIII, and Ilco does not produce a replacement 
key for this car.
Temic™: This read only chip is mainly found in European applications.
ELECTRONIC KEY SYSTEMS
EB3: This prefix refers to a key blade with a molded plastic “U-shaped” bow that is used with an electronic head to complete 
an electronic key assembly. 
EH: This prefix refers to an electronic head that contains a battery powered circuit board and is the latest version electronic head 
used for cloning transponder systems that utilize Philips® (ID46) encrypted transponders.
EH3: This prefix refers to an electronic head that contains a battery powered circuit board used for cloning  
transponder systems that utilize Texas Instruments® encrypted transponders.
EH3LB: This prefix refers to an electronic head requiring no battery used for cloning transponder systems that utilize both Texas 
Instruments® and Philips® encrypted.
EH3P: This prefix refers to an electronic head that contains a battery powered circuit board used for cloning transponder  
systems that utilize Philips® (ID46) encrypted transponders.
EK3: This prefix refers to a full electronic key assembly that includes an electronic head (EH3) and blade (EB3). It applies to 
vehicles that use Texas Instruments® encrypted transponders.
EK3P: This prefix refers to a full electronic key assembly that includes an electronic head (EH3P) and blade (EB3). It applies to 
vehicles that use Philips® (ID46) encrypted transponders. 
EK3LB: This prefix refers to a full electronic key assembly that includes an electronic head (EH3LB) and blade (EB3). 
GTH: This prefix refers to a modular head that contains a transponder used for cloning transponder systems that utilize both 
Texas Instruments® and Philips® encrypted.
GTK: This prefix refers to a full modular key assembly that includes a head (GTH) and blade (EB3). It is the latest cloning 
technology and applies to vehicles that use both Texas Instruments® and Philips® transponders.
ILCO SERVICING TOOLS
TD3AII: Transponder Detector that identifies the presence of a transponder in an automotive key.
Ilco EZ-Clone®-Clone: Cloning device for automotive transponder keys. It is a stand-alone computer with simple 2 button 
operation that allows cloning of Fixed Code Transponders and Texas Instruments® encrypted transponders.
RW4 Plus: Cloning device for automotive transponder keys. It is a stand-along computer that allows cloning of Fixed Code 
Transponders, Texas Instruments® encrypted transponders and Philips® (ID46) encrypted transponders. Also identifies the 
presence of a transponder, transponder type, ID and manufacturer. Can generate random codes and archive customer date 
for future use.
Ilco EZ-Clone®-Clone Plus: Cloning device for automotive transponder keys. It is a stand-alone computer that allows cloning of 
Fixed Code Transponders, Texas Instruments® encrypted transponders and Philips® (ID46) encrypted transponders.
Plus Box: Hardware unit that attaches to RW4 or Ilco EZ-Clone®-Clone to add the capability to clone Philips® (ID46) encrypted 
transponders.
Snoop: Device use the RW4 Plus, Ilco EZ-Clone®-Clone Plus, RW4 with Plus Box or Ilco EZ-Clone®-Clone with Plus Box that captures  
communication between the vehicle and the key when cloning Philips® (ID46) encrypted transponders.
TKO: Programming Tool for servicing vehicles when all keys have been lost, cannot be cloned or the manufacturer doesn’t 
allow programming keys through On-Board Programming. Comes loaded will all software released by Ilco through specified 
date. Fully upgradeable for future software released by Ilco.
TKO Select: Programming Tool for servicing vehicles when all keys have been lost, cannot be cloned  or the manufacturer 
doesn’t allow programming keys through On-Board Programming. This version comes pre-loaded with 15 pieces of very  
common software and is designed to be customized, by the customer, with further Ilco software to meet specific market 
demands.
TCP (T-Code Pro): Programming Tool for servicing vehicles when all keys have been lost, cannot be cloned or the  
manufacturer doesn’t allow programming keys through On-Board Programming. Comes loaded will all software released by Ilco 
through specified date. Fully upgradeable for future software released by Ilco.
MVPP (MVP Pro): Programming Tool for servicing vehicles when all keys have been lost, cannot be cloned or the manufacturer 
doesn’t allow programming keys through On-Board Programming. Comes loaded will all software released by Ilco through 
specified date. Fully upgradeable for future software released by Ilco. This is a “Pay Per Use” tool.

HOW TO USE THE AUTO/TRUCK KEY BLANK REFERENCE
1. Two indexes are provided; the MANUFACTURER INDEX and the MODEL INDEX. Both indexes are 
in alphabetical order. The Manufacturer Index references brands like Toyota, Dodge and BMW. The 
model index lists models like the Camry (Toyota), Ram (Dodge) and 3 Series (BMW). Both indexes 
tell the user on what page the reference information will be found.
2. The body of the Reference explains Manufacturer, Model, Years, Lock Applications (i.e. ignition, 
door/truck, etc.) and Code Series.  The Ilco/EZ number is the key number. A [P] indicates the key 
is available with a plastic head and a [PC] indicates the key is available in various plastic colors.  
The Transponder Information column provides pertinent information to producing the transponder 
key such as special equipment or which on board program (OBP) should be used. The Substitutes  
column provides other key blanks that should work in the application if the referenced key blank is 
not available and the Notes column contains information to assist you in cutting the key.  
 In the 2022 Ilco Auto/Truck Reference Guide is a column for Card No. In this column, users of our 
Futura, Ilco EZ®-Code, Ultracode, Tri Code H.S., Triax and Universal II code machine products will 
• Where no card number is given, either a suitable card number does not exist, or the key in 
question cannot be cut on the above listed equipment. 
• Where more than one card number is listed, more than one possible card exists; the correct 
card is dependent upon the key blank number required for the vehicle in question.
• In rare instances (the Kia section includes an example), in order to conform with code  
information as originally released by a manufacturer,   the Ilco card number requires reverse 
order depth numbering; in other words, the smaller depth bit numbers are deeper cuts than 
the larger depth bit numbers. On affected cards, if your source for bitting information utilized 
conventional depth numbering (smallest depth number = shallowest cut), you will have to 
invert their depth numbers before using the listed card number. Ilco has no control over how 
others publish code information, and assumes no liability for keys miscut as a result. 
  3. CLONING QUICK REFERENCE - A list of the vehicles/models known to  incorporate transponder 
technology that use an RW4 Plus / Ilco EZ ®-Clone device.
4. TRANSPONDER ON-BOARD PROGRAMMING PROCEDURES - This section explains the  
on-board programming procedures for installing the GM, Ford, Mazda, Toyota, Lexus and Chrysler  
programmable transponder keys that are referenced in the Auto/Truck.
5. TRANSPONDER KEYS - Actual size drawings of all transponder keys
6. 
By learning to use this reference, you can reduce the confusion over which key blank to use in an  
automobile or truck. Recognize that there will be exceptions to what is considered standard. Before cutting 
a replacement key, always compare the key blank to be cut with the original key.
IMPORTANT: Before ordering key blanks for your key boards, reference the Notes Column to see if 
the key blank is a High Security Key and requires a special key machine.  Be certain you have the key 
machine to cut the key before ordering the key blanks.
This book is provided as a service and is intended for reference only. Kaba Ilco Corp. disclaims liability for any damage or action resulting from the use of this 
information.

driven by Info Quest, the Advanced Diagnostics online key programming 
database with information for over 5000 vehicles; covering most makes and 
model worldwide.
The electronic key cutting machine with one cutting station and two 
interchangeable clamps for duplicating and originating all types of automotive 
keys, including heavy trucks and motorcycles.  Additional keys used for gas cap 
locks, glove boxes and roof racks are also included in the database.

guides the user step-by-step in all key cutting operations making it the perfect
machine for those just getting into the automotive locksmith business or the
